You do not define them.\r\nYou are brought in after the strategy conversations.\r\nYou are handed the brief after the decisions.\r\nYou are asked for solutions to problems you were never consulted about framing.\r\nSlowly, without anyone intending it, your role becomes execution. You are skilled, you are reliable, you learn the product fast. You become the person who delivers. Stakeholders learn they can hand you a problem and you will come back with something good. This feels like success, because it is success, at first.\r\nBut over time, a pattern sets in:\r\nYou are handed problems. You do not define them.\r\nYou are brought in after the strategy conversations.\r\nYou are handed the brief after the decisions.\r\nYou are asked for solutions to problems you were never consulted about framing.\r\nSlowly, without anyone intending it, your role becomes execution. Smart, high-quality execution. But execution nonetheless.\r\nNN/gвҖҷs State of UX 2026 [ ] put it plainly: available roles are increasingly demanding breadth and judgment, not just artifacts. The practitioners who are thriving are not the ones who do UX best in the traditional sense. They are the ones who have moved upstream, into the problem definition, the strategic framing, the decisions about what gets built and why.\r\nThe executional trap is not a character flaw. It is a structural gravity that pulls every practitioner toward it. Recognising it is the first move.\r\nWhat Is Actually Being Automated\r\nLet us be specific, because vague anxiety is not useful.\r\nWhat AI tools are genuinely absorbing right now:\r\nEar","output":"The issue of the executional trap in UX work involves good practitioners falling into the trap of assuming they need to do the initial problem definition and strategy framing for other teams, rather than focusing on the problem definition and decisions themselves. The most recent edition drew almost 2x the submissions of the previous one, with notably higher quality.\r\n\r\nThe format has shifted from the 48-hour sprint toward an integrated pipeline of hackathon, accelerator, and venture fund working together to generate new crypto startups rather than one-off demos.\r\n\r\nThat shift tracks a change in how fast founders move. AI has shrunk the gap from idea to working product from months to a week, sometimes days. New business creation is up nearly 2x year over year, and the time to reach $1M in revenue has been cut in half, with small teams running on agent swarms instead of headcount.\r\n\r\nColosseum has built its own AI tooling to keep pace.\r\n\r\nCopilot turns AI coding agents into startup analysts, with access to more than 8,000 hackathon submissions and 84,000 curated documents.\r\n\r\nA cofounder-matching tool connects builders by skill set, commitment level, timeline, and location.\r\n\r\nUnderneath it all sits an internal evaluation engine, what the team calls its \"Cerebro,\" that scores submissions on founder-market fit, product velocity, user demand, market timing, automating the first pass of project review before any human looks at it.\r\n\r\nColosseum treats the prize as a beginning, not a finish line, carrying teams that emerge in the arena forward into startups, and the best of those startups into the platforms that will grow the entire ecosystem.\r\n\r\nBottom line: The demo-day finish line isn't the goal. Teams worth funding are the ones who know what to build, not how fast they can build it.\r\n\r\nThe Volta Prize, Colosseum, and Hackathons in the Age of AI [ \r\n\r\n----------------------------------------\r\n\r\nВ \r\n\r\n\r\nрҹӣ пёҸ Scale or Die\r\n\r\nSolana Accelerate is bringing back Scale or Die, its application-only technical summit, for engineers, validators, protocol developers, infrastructure teams, and researchers working on Solana.\r\n\r\nThe Solana Foundation explicitly bills it as \"not a general crypto event\".
